[3:5:344,482] services are provided to California's vulnerable 

[3:6:344,492] and at-risk residents, including children and 

[3:7:344,502] adults, in ways that promote health and well-

[3:8:344,512] being, strengthen and preserve families, 

[3:9:344,522] encourage personal responsibility, and foster 

[3:10:344,532] independence.

[3:0:66,65] The Council administers grants to community-based organizations that fund new and innovative community program 

[3:1:66,75] development projects to implement State Plan objectives and improve and enhance services for individuals with developmental 

[3:2:66,85] disabilities and their families. 

[3:3:66,103] 3810 - REGIONAL OFFICES AND REGIONAL ADVISORY COMMITTEES 

[3:4:66,121] Twelve Regional Offices and Regional Advisory Committees provide administrative support and assist with advocacy, training, 

[3:5:66,131] coordination, and implementation of State Plan objectives in Council Regions throughout California. These offices and advisory 

[3:6:66,141] committees provide information and data to the Council to assess regional needs and implementation of the State Plan and for 

[3:7:66,151] inclusion in reports to the federal government and the Legislature. 

[3:8:66,169] In addition to implementation of State Plan activities, Regional Office staff support the following activities to improve and 

[3:9:66,179] enhance the availability and quality of services for residents of state developmental centers and state-operated community 

[3:10:66,189] facilities: 

[4:0:65,207] •   Advocacy services through volunteers recruited by Council staff for individuals who have no legally appointed representative 

[4:1:76,217] to assist them in making choices and decisions. 

[4:2:65,235] •   Clients' rights advocacy services to ensure that laws, regulations, and policies pertaining to the rights of persons with 

[4:3:76,245] developmental disabilities are observed. 

[4:4:65,263] •   Quality Assessments for individuals who receive community residential services and support.

[0:0:66,24] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:416,24] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   5 

[2:0:141,38] 4120   Emergency Medical Services Authority - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] Disaster Medical Services Division 

[4:0:66,83] The Disaster Medical Services Division coordinates California's medical response to major disasters by carrying out the 

[4:1:66,93] Authority's mandate to provide medical resources to local governments in support of their disaster response efforts. The 

[4:2:66,103] Division coordinates with the Governor's Office of Emergency Services, the Office of Homeland Security, the California National 

[4:3:66,113] Guard, the California Department of Public Health, and other local, state, and federal agencies, private sector hospitals, 

[4:4:66,123] ambulance companies, and medical supply vendors, to promote and improve disaster preparedness and emergency medical 

[4:5:66,134] response in California. 

[5:0:66,151] Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division 

[6:0:66,169] The Personnel Division is responsible for licensing and enforcement actions of all active paramedics throughout the state. The 

[6:1:66,179] Division develops and implements regulations that set training standards and the scope of practice for various levels of 

[6:2:66,189] personnel; sets standards for and approves training programs in pediatric first aid, CPR, and preventive health practices for 

[6:3:66,200] child day care providers and school bus drivers; and develops standards for emergency medical dispatcher training, pre-arrival 

[6:4:66,210] emergency care instructions, and the epinephrine auto-injector training program. 

[6:5:66,227] Emergency Medical Services Systems Division 

[7:0:66,245] The Systems Division is in charge of developing and implementing Emergency Medical Services systems throughout 

[7:1:66,255] California, including supporting local Health Information Exchange projects that will allow the State to collect more meaningful 

[7:2:66,266] data so that emergency medical services providers can deliver better patient care. The Division oversees system development 

[7:3:66,276] and implementation by the local Emergency Medical Services agencies, the statewide trauma system, and emergency medical 

[7:4:66,286] dispatcher and communication standards. It establishes regulations and guidelines for local agencies, reviews and approves 

[7:5:66,296] local plans to ensure they meet the minimum state standards, coordinates injury and illness prevention activities with the 

[7:6:66,306] California Department of Public Health and the Office of Traffic Safety, manages the state's Emergency Medical Services data 

[7:7:66,317] and quality improvement process, conducts Ambulance Exclusive Operating Area evaluations, and oversees the operation of 

[7:8:66,327] California's Poison Control System and Emergency Medical Services for Children programs.

[9:0:66,596] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[9:1:66,614] 3835 - HEALTH CARE WORKFORCE 

[10:0:66,631] The Health Care Workforce Program, through the Health Care Workforce Development Division and the Health Professions 

[10:1:66,642] Education Foundation, improves access to medical, mental, and dental health care providers in underserved areas throughout 

[10:2:66,652] California. The Program conducts research to identify areas of unmet need and administers grants that provide financial 

[10:3:66,662] incentives to individuals and institutions to increase the number of providers in those areas. The Program promotes health care 

[10:4:66,672] workforce diversity and cultural competency. It includes the following programs: 

[10:5:65,690] •   Song-Brown Health Care Workforce Training Program 

[10:6:65,706] •   Mental Health Services Act Workforce Education and Training Program

[4:1:66,164] 3840 - FACILITIES DEVELOPMENT 

[5:0:66,181] The Facilities Development Program safeguards public health, safety, and general welfare through regulation of the design and 

[5:1:66,191] construction of health care facilities, including compliance with seismic safety requirements, to ensure they are capable of 

[5:2:66,202] providing sustained services to the public. 

[5:3:66,219] 3845 - CAL-MORTGAGE LOAN INSURANCE 

[6:0:66,237] The Cal-Mortgage Program is modeled after federal home mortgage insurance programs and insures loans to public and 

[6:1:66,247] nonprofit health care facilities for construction, renovation, and expansion projects. The Program underwrites loans, monitors 

[6:2:66,257] the Cal-Mortgage insured loan portfolio, and administers the Health Facility Construction Loan Insurance Fund. By facilitating 

[6:3:66,268] access to private capital at no cost to taxpayers, the Program has improved the delivery of health care throughout California. 

[6:4:66,285] 3855 - HEALTH CARE INFORMATION AND QUALITY ANALYSIS 

[7:0:66,303] The Health Care Information Program sets standards for, collects, and maintains financial and utilization data from 

[7:1:66,313] approximately 6,000 licensed health facilities in California, as well as comprehensive demographic, diagnostic, and treatment 

[7:2:66,323] data for all patients discharged from licensed hospitals, treated in emergency departments, or having had an ambulatory 

[7:3:66,334] surgery procedure in hospital surgical clinics. This information is used by health care policymakers, health care providers, 

[7:4:66,344] health planners, public and private sector health care purchasers, researchers, consumers, and the media.

[0:0:66,13] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   22   HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:184,43] 4150   Department of Managed Health Care 

[2:0:66,64] The Department of Managed Health Care protects consumers' health care rights and ensures a stable health care delivery 

[2:1:66,74] system in California. The Department achieves this mission by: 

[3:0:65,92] •   Licensing and regulating managed health care plans, including all Health Maintenance Organizations (HMOs), some 

[3:1:76,102] Preferred Provider Organizations (PPOs), Exclusive Provider Organizations (EPOs), Medicare Advantage, most Medi-Cal 

[3:2:76,112] managed care plans, and specialized plans. 

[3:3:65,129] •   Enforcing the Knox-Keene Health Care Service Plan Act of 1975, as amended. 

[3:4:65,145] •   Conducting medical surveys and financial examinations to verify that health plans are complying with the law and are 

[3:5:76,155] financially stable to serve their enrollees. 

[4:0:65,171] •   Operating a 24-hour-a-day Help Center to resolve health care consumer complaints and administer the Independent Medical 

[4:1:76,181] Review program. 

[5:0:65,198] •   Reviewing proposed health plan rate changes for sufficient justification and reasonableness. 

[5:1:65,214] •   Monitoring the financial solvency of the medical groups with whom health plans contract to provide health benefits to their 

[5:2:76,224] enrollees. 

[6:0:65,240] •   Convening the Financial Solvency Standards Board, comprised of people with expertise in the medical, financial and health 

[6:1:76,250] plan industries, to advise the Director on strategies to keep the managed care industry financially stable.

[4:0:66,211] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[4:1:66,229] 3870 - HEALTH PLAN PROGRAM 

[5:0:66,249] The Health Plan Program's primary objective is to regulate managed health care plans and assist consumers to resolve 

[5:1:66,260] disputes with health plans. The program's key functions to achieve this objective are to: license managed health care plans, 

[5:2:66,270] conduct routine and non-routine financial exams and medical surveys, review proposed premium rate increases, assist 

[5:3:66,280] consumers with health care issues and enable managed health care patients to receive the medical care and services to which 

[5:4:66,290] they are entitled, and operate a consumer services toll-free complaint line (1-888-466-2219).

[0:0:66,13] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   26   HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:228,43] 4170   Department of Aging 

[1:1:66,64] The Department of Aging's mission is to promote the independence and well-being of older adults, adults with disabilities, and 

[1:2:66,74] families through: 

[2:0:65,92] •   Access to information and services to improve the quality of their lives, 

[2:1:65,108] •   Opportunities for community involvement, 

[2:2:65,124] •   Support to family members providing care, and 

[2:3:65,141] •   Collaboration with other state and local agencies. 

[3:0:66,158] As the federally designated State Unit on Aging, the Department administers federal Older Americans Act programs that 

[3:1:66,168] provide a wide variety of community-based supportive services and administers the Health Insurance Counseling and 

[3:2:66,179] Advocacy Program. The Department also administers two Medi-Cal programs: it contracts directly with agencies that operate 

[3:3:66,189] the Multipurpose Senior Services Program (MSSP) and provides oversight for the MSSP waiver, and certifies Community-

[3:4:66,199] Based Adult Services centers for participation in Medicaid. 

[4:0:66,217] The Department administers most of these programs through contracts with the state's 33 local Area Agencies on Aging. At the 

[4:1:66,227] local level, Area Agencies on Aging contract for and coordinate this array of community-based services to older adults, adults 

[4:2:66,237] with disabilities, family caregivers, and residents of long-term care facilities.

[10:0:66,564] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[10:1:66,582] 3890 - NUTRITION 

[11:0:66,600] The Nutrition Program provides nutritionally-balanced meals, nutrition education, and nutrition counseling to individuals 60 

[11:1:66,610] years of age or older. In addition to promoting better health through improved nutrition, the program focuses on reducing the 

[11:2:66,620] isolation of the elderly and providing a link to other social and supportive services such as transportation, information and 

[11:3:66,630] assistance, employment, and education. 

[11:4:66,648] 3895 - SENIOR COMMUNITY EMPLOYMENT SERVICE 

[12:0:66,666] The federal Senior Community Service Employment Program, Title V of the Older Americans Act, provides part-time subsidized 

[12:1:66,676] training and employment in community service agencies for low-income persons 55 years of age and older. The program also 

[12:2:66,686] promotes transition to unsubsidized employment.

[0:0:66,24] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   28 

[1:0:419,24] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:193,38] 4170   Department of Aging - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] This program provides supportive services in the community to adults 60 years of age or older, their family caregivers, 

[3:1:66,75] grandparents caring for grandchildren, and residents of long-term care facilities. Services include information and assistance, 

[3:2:66,85] legal assistance, transportation, respite in-home support, senior center activities, elder abuse prevention, and the Long-Term 

[3:3:66,95] Care Ombudsman. Older Americans Act Titles III and VII fund these services to enable individuals to access the support 

[3:4:66,106] necessary for them to remain independent in their communities, continue in their caregiving role, and/or receive long-term care 

[3:5:66,116] services appropriate to their needs. 

[4:0:66,134] 3905 - COMMUNITY-BASED PROGRAMS AND PROJECTS 

[5:0:66,151] This program includes the community-based Health Insurance Counseling and Advocacy Program (HICAP). HICAP provides 

[5:1:66,161] personalized counseling, community education, and outreach events for Medicare beneficiaries. HICAP is the primary local 

[5:2:66,172] source for accurate and objective information and assistance with Medicare benefits, prescription drug plans, and health plans. 

[5:3:66,189] 3910 - MEDI-CAL PROGRAMS 

[6:0:66,207] This program includes oversight of the Multipurpose Senior Services Program (MSSP) and Community-Based Adult Services 

[6:1:66,217] (CBAS) program. CBAS is a community-based day health program that provides services to adults 18 years of age or over who 

[6:2:66,227] are at risk of needing institutional care due to chronic medical, cognitive, or mental health conditions and/or disabilities. The 

[6:3:66,238] Department certifies CBAS centers for participation in the Medi-Cal Program. Under a 1915(c) Medicaid home and community-

[6:4:66,248] based services waiver, MSSP provides health and social care management to prevent premature and unnecessary long-term 

[6:5:66,258] care institutionalization of frail adults aged 65 or older who otherwise would be placed in a nursing facility.

[12:0:66,567] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[12:1:66,585] 3930 - COMMISSION ON AGING 

[13:0:66,603] The Commission's statutory responsibilities include: assisting with the development of the Department of Aging's State Plan on 

[13:1:66,613] Aging, monitoring the plan's progress, and information-gathering. As part of its information-gathering responsibility, the 

[13:2:66,623] Commission holds meetings and public hearings around the state to address the issues and concerns of older Californians, 

[13:3:66,634] their families, and caregivers. The Commission uses the information gathered from these meetings and public hearings to 

[13:4:66,644] develop initiatives and projects focused on older Californians and their caregivers. The Commission also assisted with the 

[13:5:66,654] development and implementation of the state's Alzheimer's Disease Plan, holds membership on the California Family 

[14:0:66,664] Caregiver Task Force, and administers the Area Agency on Aging Council of California. The Area Agency on Aging Council of 

[14:1:66,674] California is supported solely by voluntary contributions made through a check-off box included on the state income tax form.

[0:0:66,13] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   48   HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:169,43] 4260   State Department of Health Care Services 

[2:0:66,64] The mission of the California Department of Health Care Services (DHCS) is to provide Californians with access to affordable, 

[2:1:66,74] integrated, high-quality health care including medical, dental, mental health, substance use disorder services, and long-term 

[2:2:66,84] care. To fulfill its mission, DHCS finances and administers a number of individual health care service delivery programs, 

[3:0:66,95] including the state's Medicaid Program (Medi-Cal), which provides health care services to low-income persons and families 

[3:1:66,105] who meet defined eligibility requirements. 

[4:0:66,123] To achieve its mission, DHCS has set the following goals: 

[4:1:65,140] •   Organize care to promote improved health outcomes. 

[4:2:65,156] •   Promote comprehensive health coverage. 

[5:0:65,173] •   Measure health system performance and reward improved outcomes. 

[5:1:65,189] •   Increase accountability and fiscal integrity. 

[6:0:65,205] •   Encourage the viability and availability of safety net services.

[3:1:76,75] funding at 88 percent through September 30, 2019, phasing down in future years to the historic ratio of 65 percent. 

[4:0:65,91] •   ACA Optional Expansion—In January of each year, the state’s cost-sharing ratio for the 3.9 million Californians in the 

[4:1:76,101] optional Medi-Cal expansion increases incrementally until it reaches 10 percent in 2020. The Budget includes $18.7 billion 

[4:2:76,112] ($1.7 billion General Fund), an increase of $803.2 million ($251 million General Fund) compared to 2017-18 for the optional 

[4:3:76,122] expansion population. 

[5:0:65,138] •   Elimination of State-Only Limits on Breast and Cervical Cancer Treatment—The Budget includes $8.4 million General Fund 

[5:1:76,148] to eliminate the 18-month treatment limitation for breast cancer and 24-month treatment limitation for cervical cancer in the 

[5:2:76,158] state-only Breast and Cervical Cancer Treatment Program. 

[6:0:65,175] •   Data Collection and Sharing Initiatives—The Budget includes $50 million ($5 million General Fund) in 2018-19 for the 

[6:1:76,185] development of Health Information Exchanges to facilitate data sharing of health information between health systems. It also 

[6:2:76,195] includes funding for changes to the California Health Information Survey to study the accuracy of responses and data 

[6:3:76,205] collected related to children's health ($750,00 General Fund) and for incorporating questions and increasing efforts to 

[6:4:76,215] conduct outreach involving long-term services and supports ($3 million General Fund). 

[7:0:65,232] •   Expand Hepatitis C Treatment Clinical Guidelines—The Budget includes $70.4 million ($21.8 million General Fund) in 

[7:1:76,242] 2018-19 to authorize treatment for all patients ages 13 and above with Hepatitis C, regardless of liver fibrosis state or co-

[7:2:76,252] morbidity, except for patients with a life expectancy of less than 12 months. 

[8:0:65,268] •   Homeless Mentally Ill Outreach and Treatment—The Budget includes a one-time augmentation of $50 million for the 

[8:1:76,278] Department of Health Care Services to provide counties with targeted funding for multi-disciplinary teams to provide 

[8:2:76,289] intensive outreach, treatment and related services for homeless persons with mental illness. This type of intervention is 

[8:3:76,299] expected to result in earlier identification of mental health needs, prevention of criminal justice involvement, and better 

[8:4:76,309] coordination of care for this population at the local level. 

[9:0:65,325] •   Restoration of Medi-Cal Dental Benefit—The Budget includes $209.7 million ($63.7 million General Fund) for the restoration 

[9:1:76,335] of full dental services for adult beneficiaries in the Medi-Cal program, which became effective January 1, 2018. 

[10:0:65,352] •   Medi-Cal County Administration—The Budget includes an increase of $56.6 million ($19.0 General Fund) based on adjusting 

[10:1:76,362] the existing level of funding by the California Price Index.

[5:0:66,255] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[6:0:66,273] 3960010 - MEDICAL CARE SERVICES (MEDI-CAL) 

[7:0:66,291] Medi-Cal is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income Californians. Medi-Cal 

[7:1:66,301] provides access to quality medical care in a fiscally prudent manner through both fee-for-service and managed care delivery 

[7:2:66,311] systems. Medi-Cal activities are carried out through the following divisions: Integrated Systems of Care; Managed Care Quality 

[7:3:66,322] and Monitoring; Managed Care Operations; Medi-Cal Eligibility; Medi-Cal Dental Services; Pharmacy Benefits; Benefits; Safety 

[7:4:66,332] Net Financing; Capitated Rates Development; Fee-For-Service Rates Development; Mental Health Services; Substance Use 

[7:5:66,342] Disorder Compliance; Substance Use Disorder Program, Policy, and Fiscal; Fiscal Forecasting; Audits and Investigations; 

[7:6:66,352] California Medicaid Management Information Systems; Provider Enrollment; Research and Analytic Studies; Third Party 

[7:7:66,362] Liability and Recovery; Information Management; and Clinical Assurance and Administrative Support. Additionally Program 

[7:8:66,373] Offices include: the Office of Medi-Cal Procurement; and the Office of Family Planning. 

[7:9:66,390] 3960023 - CHILDREN'S MEDICAL SERVICES 

[8:0:66,408] Children's Medical Services is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income and 

[8:1:66,418] seriously ill children, including the Child Health and Disability Prevention Program, the Genetically Handicapped Persons 

[8:2:66,428] Program, and the California Children's Services Program. These services are provided by the Integrated Systems of Care 

[8:3:66,439] Division. 

[9:0:66,456] 3960032 - PRIMARY, RURAL, AND INDIAN HEALTH 

[10:0:66,474] Primary, Rural, and Indian Health is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care to Californians in rural 

[10:1:66,484] areas and to underserved populations through the following programs: Indian Health Program, American Indian Infant Health 

[10:2:66,494] Initiative, Rural Health Services Development Program, Seasonal Agricultural and Migratory Workers Program, State Office of 

[10:3:66,505] Rural Health, Medicare Rural Hospital Flexibility Program, Small Rural Hospital Improvement Grant Program, Tribal Emergency 

[10:4:66,515] Preparedness Program, and the J1 Visa Program. 

[10:5:66,532] 3960050 - OTHER CARE SERVICES 

[11:0:66,550] The Department is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of non Medi-Cal community mental health services 

[11:1:66,560] and substance use disorder services: cancer screening services to low-income, under-insured, or uninsured women; and 

[11:2:66,571] prostate cancer treatment services to low-income, under-insured, or uninsured men. These services are provided through the 

[11:3:66,581] Mental Health Services Division, Substance Use Disorder Compliance Division, the Every Woman Counts Program, and the 

[11:4:66,591] Prostate Cancer Treatment Program. 

[11:5:66,609] 9900100 - DEPARTMENTAL ADMINISTRATION 

[12:0:66,626] This program provides overall management, planning, policy development, legal and administrative support for all DHCS 

[12:1:66,637] programs. This program is carried out by the Executive Division, the Office of Administrative Hearings and Appeals, the Office 

[12:2:66,647] of Legal Services, the Office of Civil Rights, the Legislative and Governmental Affairs, the Office of Communications, the 

[12:3:66,657] Enterprise Innovation & Technology Services Division, and the Administration Division. 

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:0:207,43] 4265   Department of Public Health 

[2:0:66,64] The California Department of Public Health (Public Health) is dedicated to optimizing the health and well-being of all 

[2:1:66,74] Californians through the following core activities: 

[3:0:65,92] •   Protecting the public from communicable diseases. 

[4:0:65,108] •   Protecting the public from unhealthy and unsafe environments. 

[5:0:65,124] •   Preventing disease, disability, and premature death; and reducing or eliminating health disparities. 

[5:1:65,141] •   Preparing for and responding to public health emergencies. 

[6:0:65,157] •   Producing and disseminating data to evaluate population health status, inform people, institutions and communities; and to 

[6:1:76,167] guide public health strategies, programs, and actions. 

[7:0:65,183] •   Promoting healthy lifestyles for individuals and families in their communities and workplaces. 

[7:1:65,199] •   Providing access to quality, population-based health services. 

[8:0:66,217] Because Public Health's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to 

[8:1:66,227] support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[6:0:66,316] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES 

[7:0:65,334] •   Licensing and Certification: Los Angeles County Contract Extension - The Budget includes $2.6 million Licensing and 

[7:1:76,344] Certification Fund for a one-year extension of Public Health's contract with the Los Angeles County Department of Public 

[7:2:76,355] Health to perform licensing and certification activities in Los Angeles County. The Budget also includes provisional language 

[7:3:76,365] to augment expenditures and revenues by up to $1.3 million if Public Health demonstrates a need for additional resources 

[7:4:76,375] for its contract with the County. Additionally, the Budget includes trailer bill language allowing Public Health to assess and 

[7:5:76,385] apply a supplemental fee to its regulated health care entities located in Los Angeles County beginning in 2018-19. This fee 

[7:6:76,395] will be based on the additional cost necessary to administer and enforce licensing and certification services to health care 

[7:7:76,406] entities located in the County. 

[8:0:65,422] •   Public Health Investments - The Budget includes $11.4 million General Fund for the following ongoing health expenditures: 

[8:1:76,432] expansion of Black Infant Health Program services in the California Perinatal Equity Initiative ($8 million); Alzheimer’s 

[8:2:76,442] disease research ($3.1 million); and $300,000 to backfill a loss of federal funds for the Office of Binational Border Health. 

[8:3:76,452] The Budget also includes $23.5 million General Fund for the following one-time public health expenditures: services for 

[8:4:76,463] individuals diagnosed with Amyotrophic Lateral Sclerosis ($9 million); human immunodeficiency virus prevention ($5 million); 

[8:5:76,473] outreach and research for valley fever ($5 million); diabetes prevention and treatment ($2.5 million); and sexually transmitted 

[8:6:76,483] disease prevention ($2 million). 

[9:0:65,499] •   Implementation of the Medicinal and Adult Use Cannabis and Regulation Safety Act - The Budget includes $11.1 million and 

[9:1:76,509] 28.5 positions in 2018-19 for Public Health to continue implementing the requirements of the Act. 

[10:0:65,526] •   Childhood Trauma - The Budget includes $10 million one-time Mental Health Services Fund for Public Health to support a 

[10:1:76,536] three-year All Children Thrive pilot program to address childhood trauma. This targeted investment will be used to provide up 

[10:2:76,546] to 12 cities and counties with grants to implement local public health strategies to prevent childhood trauma.

[0:0:66,24] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES

[2:0:172,38] 4265   Department of Public Health - Continued 

[3:0:66,74] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[4:0:66,92] 4040010 - Emergency Preparedness 

[5:0:66,102] The Public Health Emergency Preparedness program coordinates preparedness and response activities for all public health 

[5:1:66,113] emergencies, including natural disasters, acts of terrorism, and pandemic diseases. The program plans and supports surge 

[5:2:66,123] capacity in the medical care and public health systems to meet needs during emergencies. The program also administers 

[5:3:66,133] federal and state funds that support Public Health emergency preparedness activities. 

[6:0:66,151] 4045 - PUBLIC AND ENVIRONMENTAL HEALTH 

[7:0:66,161] The Public and Environmental Health programs provide public health services of: communicable disease control; chronic 

[7:1:66,171] disease and injury prevention; environmental public health; maternal, child, and family health; and vital records. These 

[7:2:66,181] programs function as part of the greater public health system throughout California. 

[8:0:66,199] 4045010 - Chronic Disease Prevention and Health Promotion 

[9:0:66,217] This program works to prevent and control chronic diseases, injuries, and violence. Chronic diseases include cancer, 

[9:1:66,227] cardiovascular diseases, asthma, and diabetes. The areas of focus for this program include: reducing the prevalence of 

[9:2:66,237] obesity; reducing and preventing tobacco use; developing the local public health workforce; preventing and controlling injuries, 

[9:3:66,247] violence, deaths, and diseases related to behavioral, environmental, and occupational factors; promoting and supporting safe 

[9:4:66,257] and healthy environments in all communities and workplaces; and preventing and treating problem gambling. This program 

[9:5:66,268] includes Chronic Disease and Injury Control, Environmental and Occupational Disease Control, and the Office of Problem 

[9:6:66,278] Gambling. 

[10:0:66,296] 4045023 - Infectious Diseases 

[11:0:66,313] This program works to prevent and control infectious diseases such as: HIV/AIDS, viral hepatitis, influenza and other vaccine-

[11:1:66,323] preventable illnesses, sexually transmitted diseases, tuberculosis, emerging infections, and foodborne illnesses. This program 

[11:2:66,334] includes Communicable Disease Control, the Office of AIDS, the Office of Binational Border Health, and the Office of Refugee 

[11:3:66,344] Health. 

[12:0:66,362] 4045032 - Family Health 

[13:0:66,379] This program works to improve and reduce disparities in health outcomes for girls and women of reproductive age, pregnant 

[13:1:66,389] and postpartum women, infants, children, and adolescents and their families. This program includes Genetic Disease 

[13:2:66,400] Screening; Maternal, Child, and Adolescent Health; and the Special Supplemental Nutrition Program for Women, Infants, and 

[13:3:66,410] Children. 

[14:0:66,428] 4045041 - Health Statistics and Informatics 

[15:0:66,445] This program develops data systems and facilitates the collection, validation, analysis, and dissemination of health information. 

[15:1:66,455] This program includes Vital Records, Public Health Policy and Research, and Public Health Informatics. 

[16:0:66,473] 4045050 - County Health Services 

[17:0:66,491] This program supports county-based public health information and services, including the Medical Marijuana Identification Card 

[17:1:66,501] Program. 

[18:0:66,519] 4045059 - Environmental Health 

[19:0:66,536] This program works to protect and improve the health of all California residents by providing for the safety of food, drugs, 

[19:1:66,547] medical devices, and manufactured cannabis products; conducting underage tobacco enforcement; conducting environmental 

[19:2:66,557] management programs; and overseeing the use of radiation through investigation, inspection, laboratory testing, and regulatory 

[19:3:66,567] activities. This program includes Environmental Management, Drinking Water and Radiation Laboratory, Food and Drug Safety, 

[19:4:66,577] Radiologic Health, Manufactured Cannabis Safety, and the Food and Drug Laboratory. 

[20:0:66,595] 4050 - LICENSING AND CERTIFICATION 

[21:0:66,613] 4050010 - Health Facilities 

[22:0:66,630] This program regulates the quality of care in over 10,000 public and private health facilities, clinics, and agencies throughout 

[22:1:66,641] the state; licenses nursing home administrators; certifies nurse assistants, home health aides, and hemodialysis technicians; 

[22:2:66,651] and oversees the prevention, surveillance and reporting of healthcare-associated infections in California's general acute care 

[22:3:66,661] hospitals. 

[23:0:66,679] 4050019 - Laboratory Field Services 

[24:0:66,696] This program regulates quality standards in approximately 22,000 clinical laboratories, public health laboratories, blood banks, 

[24:1:66,707] and tissue banks in California; and licenses approximately 60,000 scientific classifications that include 30 different categories of 

[25:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES   2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   123 

[1:0:176,43] 4300   Department of Developmental Services 

[2:0:66,64] The Department of Developmental Services is responsible under the Lanterman Developmental Disabilities Services Act for 

[2:1:66,74] providing persons with developmental disabilities the services and supports they need to lead more independent and 

[2:2:66,84] productive lives and to make choices and decisions about their lives. The Department sets broad policy and provides 

[2:3:66,95] leadership for developmental services statewide; establishes priorities, standards, and procedures within which the 

[2:4:66,105] developmental services program operates; monitors, reviews, and evaluates service delivery; and helps to remediate problems 

[2:5:66,115] that arise. Services are delivered directly through a statewide network of 21 private, nonprofit, locally based community 

[2:6:66,125] agencies known as regional centers as well as through developmental centers and a state-operated community facility. The 

[2:7:66,135] Department, through the 21 private, nonprofit regional centers, oversees coordination of services to persons with 

[2:8:66,146] developmental disabilities; provides that such services are planned, provided, and meet the needs and choices of these 

[2:9:66,156] individuals at each stage of their lives; and, to the extent possible, accomplishes these goals in the individual's home 

[2:10:66,166] community. 

[3:0:66,186] Because the Department's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to 

[3:1:66,197] support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[2:0:66,112] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES 

[3:0:65,130] •   Bridge Funding for Service Providers—The Budget includes one-time funding of $25   million General Fund in 2018-19 for a 

[3:1:76,140] targeted rate increase for direct care service staff.   The funding provides a limited-term increase in advance of the 

[3:2:76,151] department developing a 2019 rate study of the current methods for setting rates, including whether there is an adequate 

[3:3:76,161] supply of vendors; a comparison of the fiscal effects of alternative rate setting methods; and how vendor rates relate to 

[3:4:76,171] consumer outcomes. 

[3:5:65,187] •   Uniform Holiday Schedule Suspension—The Budget includes $29.3 million General Fund on a one-time basis to suspend 

[3:6:76,197] the 14-day Uniform Holiday Schedule statute in 2018-19. 

[3:7:65,214] •   Provider Rate Increase—The Budget includes an increase of $17.7 million General Fund to provide a rate increase for Home 

[3:8:76,224] Health, Intermediate Care Facility-Developmentally Disabled, and Pediatric Day Health Care providers. This adjustment is 

[3:9:76,234] consistent with increases provided in the Department of Health Care Services, Medi-Cal program. 

[3:10:65,250] •   Minimum Wage—The Budget includes an increase of $245.4 million ($133.7 million General Fund) in 2018-19 to reflect the 

[3:11:76,260] impact on providers of the state minimum wage. This amount includes the increases of the hourly wage to $12.00, effective 

[3:12:76,271] January 1, 2019.

[5:0:66,291] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[6:0:66,309] 4140 - COMMUNITY SERVICES PROGRAM 

[7:0:66,327] Through the network of regional centers, the Department supports the development and maintenance of services for eligible 

[7:1:66,337] persons with developmental disabilities who reside in the community. The regional centers directly provide or coordinate the 

[7:2:66,347] following services and supports: (1) information and referral, (2) assessment and diagnosis, (3) counseling, (4) lifelong 

[7:3:66,357] individualized planning and service coordination, (5) purchase of necessary services included in the individual program plan, 

[7:4:66,368] (6) assistance in finding and using community and other resources, (7) advocacy for the protection of legal, civil, and service 

[7:5:66,378] rights, (8) early intervention services for infants and their families, (9) family support, (10) planning, placement, and monitoring 

[7:6:66,388] for 24-hour out-of-home care, (11) training and educational opportunities for individuals and families, (12) community education 

[7:7:66,398] about developmental disabilities, and (13) habilitation services. 

[8:0:66,416] 4145 - STATE-OPERATED RESIDENTIAL AND COMMUNITY FACILITIES PROGRAM 

[9:0:66,434] The Department operates three residential facilities: Fairview Developmental Center (Orange County), Porterville 

[10:0:66,444] Developmental Center (Tulare County), and Sonoma Developmental Center (Sonoma County). Secure treatment services are 

[10:1:66,454] provided at the Porterville Developmental Center. The Department also leases one small community facility for persons who 

[10:2:66,464] require specialized behavioral interventions: Canyon Springs, a 63-bed facility in Cathedral City (Riverside County). The 

[10:3:66,474] residential facilities are licensed as General Acute Care Hospitals with distinct parts for skilled nursing care and intermediate 

[10:4:66,485] care. Canyon Springs operates as an intermediate care facility only. Services at all facilities involve the provision of active 

[10:5:66,495] treatment through residential and day programs on a 24-hour basis, including appropriate medical and dental care, health 

[10:6:66,505] maintenance activities, and assistance with activities of daily living, training, education, and employment. 

[11:0:66,523] Beginning in 2018-19, the Department will operate four Stabilization, Training, Assistance, and Reintegration (STAR) 

[12:0:66,533] residences that provide acute crisis services in the community. Individuals served in the STAR residences are committed by a 

[12:1:66,543] court order to the Department for suitable treatment and habilitation services, and are provided services and supports 

[12:2:66,553] necessary to prepare them for return to their residential home or to transition to a new living option. 

[13:0:66,571] The primary objectives of this program include providing care, treatment, crisis services, and habilitation services to residents 

[13:1:66,581] based upon assessed need and as outlined in each person's Individual Program Plan. These services are offered in the most 

[13:2:66,591] efficient, effective, and least restrictive manner to all individuals referred by the regional centers and/or the judicial system; and 

[13:3:66,602] are designed to teach individuals skills for increased independence, provide for preservation or improvement of health and 

[13:4:66,612] welfare, and enhance personal competence in all areas of daily living. 

[14:0:66,630] The Developmental Centers Division provides central administrative and clinical management services to the three 

[15:0:66,640] developmental centers and the leased small community facility to oversee the quality of services provided, compliance with 

[15:1:66,650] state licensing and federal certification requirements, protection of consumers and staff, and maintenance of facility structures 

[15:2:66,660] and grounds. Areas of responsibility include the development of policy and procedures for all aspects of the developmental 

[15:3:66,670] centers operations, law enforcement and protective services, facility population management, program and fiscal oversight, and 

[15:4:66,681] facilities planning and support. 

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES   2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   135 

[1:0:201,43] 4440   Department of State Hospitals 

[2:0:66,64] The Department of State Hospitals manages the nation's largest inpatient forensic mental health hospital system. Its mission is 

[2:1:66,74] to provide evaluation and treatment in a safe and responsible manner, seeking innovation and excellence in state hospital 

[2:2:66,84] operations, across a continuum of care. The Department is responsible for the daily care and provision of mental health 

[3:0:66,95] treatment for its patients in five state hospitals, and employs nearly 11,000 staff. Additionally, the Department provides services 

[3:1:66,105] in jail-based competency treatment programs and conditional release programs throughout the 58 counties. In 2016-17, State 

[3:2:66,115] Hospitals served approximately 13,000 patients, with an average daily inpatient census of approximately 7,000; and the jail-

[3:3:66,125] based competency programs served approximately 700 patients, with a daily capacity of around 200 beds. The conditional 

[3:4:66,135] release program maintains an average daily census of approximately 650. 

[4:0:66,156] The Department oversees five state hospitals, located in Atascadero, Coalinga, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, and Patton. 

[4:1:66,166] The psychiatric programs treating mentally-ill prisoners, operating at Vacaville, Salinas Valley, and Stockton state prisons, were 

[4:2:66,176] transferred to the California Department of Corrections and Rehabilitation as of July 1, 2017. The Department continues to 

[4:3:66,186] designate 336 beds at Atascadero, Coalinga, and Patton state hospitals for the treatment of mentally-ill Coleman class 

[4:4:66,197] prisoners. 

[5:0:66,217] Because the Department of State Hospitals' programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital 

[5:1:66,227] outlay program to support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure 

[5:2:66,237] Overview."

[4:0:66,228] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[4:1:66,246] 4380 - IN-PATIENT SERVICES PROGRAM 

[5:0:66,267] The In-Patient Services Program administers the California state hospital system, the Conditional Release Program, the Sex 

[5:1:66,277] Offender Commitment Program, the Restoration of Competency Program, and the treatment and evaluation of judicially and 

[5:2:66,287] civilly committed patients. 

[6:0:66,307] Program Administration 

[7:0:66,328] Program Administration includes headquarters functions that support the state hospital system, including policy development 

[7:1:66,338] and management, licensing oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight, data research and fiscal management. 

[8:0:66,358] In-Patient Services 

[9:0:66,379] The state hospital system includes five state hospitals: Atascadero, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, Patton, and Coalinga. In 

[9:1:66,389] addition, until July 1, 2017, this program included three inpatient psychiatric programs located at the California Medical Facility 

[9:2:66,399] in Vacaville, Salinas Valley State Prison in Salinas Valley and within the California Health Care Facility in Stockton. The three 

[9:3:66,409] psychiatric programs provide treatment services to CDCR inmates and the responsibility for these facilities transferred to 

[9:4:66,420] CDCR beginning in 2017-18. Mental health treatment services at all facilities are delivered by clinical teams who provide full-

[9:5:66,430] time inpatient care to the most serious mentally ill and those incapable of living in the community. 

[10:0:66,450] Conditional Release 

[11:0:66,471] The Conditional Release Program (CONREP) is the statewide system of community-based services for specified forensic 

[11:1:66,481] patients. Mandated as a state responsibility by the Governor's Mental Health Initiative of 1984, the program began operations 

[11:2:66,491] on January 1, 1986. 

[12:0:66,511] The goal of CONREP is to provide greater public protection in California communities via a standardized community outpatient 

[12:1:66,522] treatment system. 

[13:0:66,542] Restoration of Competency/Jail-Based Competency Treatment 

[14:0:66,562] The Restoration of Competency /Jail-Based Competency Treatment Program focuses on defendants deemed incompetent to 

[14:1:66,573] stand trial in accordance with Penal Code Section 1370. The Program provides mental health treatment to defendants in a jail-

[14:2:66,583] based or community setting, restores them to competency, and allows for participation in court proceedings. 

[14:3:66,600] 4380010 - PROGRAM ADMINISTRATION 

[15:0:66,618] Program Administration includes headquarters functions that support the state hospital system, including policy development 

[15:1:66,628] and management, licensing oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight, data research and fiscal management. 

[15:2:66,646] 4380019 - IN-PATIENT SERVICES

[0:0:66,24] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   138

[2:0:166,38] 4440   Department of State Hospitals - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] 4380028 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE 

[4:0:66,83] The Conditional Release Program (CONREP) is the statewide system of community-based services for specified forensic 

[4:1:66,93] patients. Mandated as a state responsibility by the Governor's Mental Health Initiative of 1984, the program began operations 

[4:2:66,103] on January 1, 1986. The goal of CONREP is to provide greater public protection in California communities via a standardized 

[4:3:66,113] community outpatient treatment system. 

[5:0:66,131] 4385 - FORENSIC AND EVALUATION SERVICES 

[6:0:66,149] Forensic and Evaluation Services is comprised of the Mentally Disordered Offender (MDO) and the Sex Offender Commitment 

[6:1:66,159] Program (SOCP). The MDO program applies only to prisoners whose crimes were committed on or after January 1, 1986. 

[6:2:66,169] Penal Code Sections 2960-2981 require that a prisoner who meets six specific criteria be ordered by the Board of Prison Terms 

[6:3:66,179] to be treated by State Hospitals as a condition of parole. Welfare and Institutions Code Section 6600 et seq. (Chapter 793, 

[6:4:66,189] Statutes of 1995) was enacted January 1, 1996, establishing a new category of civil commitment for persons found, upon 

[6:5:66,200] release from prison, to be sexually violent predators (SVP). The SOCP administers clinical screenings to determine whether an 

[6:6:66,210] individual is likely to be a SVP and warrants forensic psychological evaluations by the Department. 

[7:0:66,227] 4390 - LEGAL SERVICES 

[8:0:66,245] The Legal Services Division is responsible for providing a full range of comprehensive legal services including, but not limited 

[8:1:66,255] to: developing legislation; providing litigation; protecting the confidentiality and privacy of patient information under the Health 

[8:2:66,266] Information Portability and Accountability Act; providing contract law advice to the state hospitals, psychiatric programs and 

[8:3:66,276] headquarters; and representing the Department at various court and administrative law proceedings involving involuntary 

[8:4:66,286] medication, orders to show cause, and personnel actions statewide. 

[9:0:66,304] 4400 - ADMINISTRATION 

[10:0:66,321] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health 

[10:1:66,332] services to patients admitted into Department of State Hospitals facilities. Program Administration includes headquarters 

[10:2:66,342] functions such as: policy development and management, licensing oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight, 

[10:3:66,352] data research, fiscal, personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services. 

[11:0:66,370] Hospital Administration includes centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care but are administered 

[11:1:66,380] centrally from headquarters. 

[12:0:66,398] 4400010 - HEADQUARTERS ADMINISTRATION 

[13:0:66,415] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health 

[13:1:66,425] services to patients admitted into Department of State Hospitals facilities. Program Administration includes headquarters 

[13:2:66,436] functions such as: policy development and management, licensing oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight, 

[13:3:66,446] data research, fiscal, personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services. 

[14:0:66,464] 4400020 - HOSPITAL ADMINISTRATION 

[15:0:66,481] Hospital Administration includes centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care but are administered 

[15:1:66,491] centrally from headquarters.

[17:0:66,527] The state hospital system includes five state hospitals located at Atascadero, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, Patton, and 

[17:1:66,537] Coalinga. Mental health treatment services at all facilities are delivered by clinical teams who provide full-time inpatient care to 

[17:2:66,547] those with mental illness and those incapable of living in the community. The state hospitals treat the following types of 

[17:3:66,557] patients: civil commitments under the Lanterman-Petris-Short Act; forensic commitments such as incompetent to stand trial, not 

[17:4:66,568] guilty by reason of insanity, sexually violent predators, and mentally disordered offenders; and prisoners with mental illness 

[17:5:66,578] from the California Department of Corrections and Rehabilitation.

[6:3:66,245] 4440 - FORENSIC AND EVALUATION SERVICES 

[7:0:66,263] Forensic and Evaluation Services is comprised of the Mentally Disordered Offender and the Sex Offender Commitment 

[7:1:66,273] Programs. Penal Code Sections 2960-2981 require that a prisoner who meets specific criteria be ordered by the Board of 

[7:2:66,283] Prison Terms to be treated by State Hospitals as a condition of parole. The Department of State Hospitals performs evaluations 

[7:3:66,293] to determine if individuals may meet the statutory criteria for the Mentally Disordered Offender program. These evaluations are 

[7:4:66,304] used by the Board of Parole Hearings in determining whether a prisoner is committed to the Department of State Hospitals as a 

[7:5:66,314] condition of parole. Welfare and Institutions Code Section 6600 et seq. (Chapter 793, Statutes of 1995) was enacted January 

[7:6:66,324] 1, 1996, establishing a new category of civil commitment for persons found, upon release from prison, to be sexually violent 

[7:7:66,334] predators. The Sex Offender Commitment Program administers clinical screenings and performs evaluations to determine if 

[7:8:66,344] prisoners may meet the statutory criteria for a sexually violent predator commitment to the Department of State Hospitals upon 

[7:9:66,355] completion of their prison term. Superior Courts make the ultimate determination whether an individual is likely to be a sexually 

[7:10:66,365] violent predator and warrants forensic psychological evaluations by the Department of State Hospitals.

[4:0:66,127] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[5:0:66,145] 4170 - MENTAL HEALTH SERVICES OVERSIGHT AND ACCOUNTABILITY COMMISSION 

[5:1:66,163] The Commission was established to provide oversight and accountability for the Mental Health Services Act (MHSA), Adult and 

[5:2:66,173] Older Adult System of Care Act and Children's Mental Health Services Act. The Commission's primary roles include: (1) 

[5:3:66,183] providing oversight, review, accountability, and evaluation of projects and programs supported with MHSA funds, (2) assessing 

[5:4:66,194] if services that are provided pursuant to the MHSA are cost-effective and in accordance with recommended best practices, (3) 

[5:5:66,204] providing oversight and accountability of the MHSA funded community mental health system, (4) reviewing and approving 

[5:6:66,214] county Innovation Program and Expenditure Plans, (5) providing counties technical assistance in MHSA program plan 

[5:7:66,224] development to accomplish the purposes of the MHSA, and (6) administering the Mental Health Wellness Act of 2013 Triage 

[5:8:66,234] Personnel grants. The Commission also advises the Governor and the Legislature regarding state actions to improve care and 

[5:9:66,245] services for people with mental illness.

[4:0:66,266] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[4:1:66,284] 4181 - ENERGY PROGRAMS 

[5:0:66,302] The Energy Programs assist low-income households in meeting their immediate and long-term home energy needs through 

[5:1:66,312] financial assistance, energy conservation, weatherization and renewable energy services. 

[6:0:66,330] The Low-Income Home Energy Assistance Program (LIHEAP) provides financial assistance to eligible low-income households 

[6:1:66,340] to offset the costs of heating and/or cooling residential dwellings, assistance for weather-related or energy-related 

[6:2:66,350] emergencies, and weatherization services to improve the energy efficiency of low-income residential dwellings and safeguard 

[6:3:66,360] the health and safety of household occupants. This program may include a leveraging incentive program in which 

[6:4:66,370] supplementary LIHEAP funds can be obtained by LIHEAP grantees if non-federal leveraged home energy resources are used 

[6:5:66,381] along with LIHEAP weatherization related services. 

[7:0:66,398] The Department of Energy Weatherization Assistance Program provides weatherization to improve the energy efficiency of low-

[7:1:66,408] income residential dwellings and safeguard the health and safety of household occupants. 

[8:0:66,426] The Lead-Based Paint Hazard Control Program provides services to fully abate or control lead paint hazards in low-income 

[8:1:66,436] privately owned housing with young children. 

[9:0:66,454] The Low-Income Weatherization Program (LIWP) provides weatherization and renewable energy services in low-income 

[9:1:66,464] single-family and multi-family dwellings within disadvantaged communities to help reduce greenhouse gas emissions. LIWP 

[9:2:66,474] includes projects such as weatherization and solar water heater and solar photovoltaic systems installations. 

[9:3:66,492] 4185 - COMMUNITY SERVICES 

[10:0:66,510] The Community Services Block Grant is designed to enable local government and private nonprofit community organizations to 

[10:1:66,520] help low-income families achieve and maintain self-sufficiency through a broad range of activities. These activities include 

[10:2:66,530] education, employment services, emergency services, housing, income support and management, and health and nutritional 

[10:3:66,540] services. Additionally, Community Services Block Grant funds are used by local community organizations to revitalize low-

[10:4:66,551] income communities. 

[11:0:66,591] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[0:0:66,24] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:407,24] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   165 

[2:0:170,38] 5160   Department of Rehabilitation - Continued 

[3:0:66,72] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[4:0:66,91] 4210 - VOCATIONAL REHABILITATION SERVICES 

[5:0:66,108] The Vocational Rehabilitation Services Program delivers vocational rehabilitation services to persons with disabilities through 

[5:1:66,119] vocational rehabilitation professionals in district and branch offices located throughout the state. In addition, the Department 

[5:2:66,129] has cooperative agreements with state and local agencies (education, mental health, and welfare) to provide services to 

[5:3:66,139] consumers. The Department operates under a federal Order of Selection process, which gives priority to persons with the most 

[5:4:66,149] significant disabilities. 

[6:0:66,167] Persons with disabilities who are eligible for the Department's vocational rehabilitation services may be provided a full range of 

[6:1:66,177] services, including vocational assessment, assistive technology, vocational and educational training, job placement, and 

[6:2:66,187] independent living skills training to maximize their ability to live and work independently within their communities. 

[7:0:66,205] The Department provides comprehensive training and technical assistance to enable persons who are blind or visually 

[7:1:66,215] impaired to support themselves in the operation of vending stands, snack bars, and cafeterias. Prevocational services are 

[7:2:66,225] provided by the Orientation Center for the Blind to newly blind adults to prepare them for vocational rehabilitation services and 

[7:3:66,236] independent living. 

[8:0:66,253] The Department works with public and private organizations to develop and improve community-based vocational rehabilitation 

[8:1:66,263] services for the Department's consumers. The Department sets standards, certifies Community Rehabilitation Programs, and 

[8:2:66,274] establishes fees for services provided to its consumers. 

[9:0:66,291] The Department works with the federal government to administer two grant programs. The Promoting the Readiness of Minors 

[9:1:66,302] in Supplemental Security Income grant develops projects to promote positive outcomes for children who receive Supplemental 

[9:2:66,312] Security Income and their families. The CA Innovations Program seeks to increase the self-sufficiency of students with 

[9:3:66,322] disabilities by providing work-based learning experiences and planned education to prepare them for workplace success. 

[10:0:66,340] 4215 - INDEPENDENT LIVING SERVICES 

[11:0:66,357] The Department funds, administers, and supports 28 non-profit independent living centers in communities located throughout 

[11:1:66,368] California. Each independent living center provides services necessary to assist consumers to live independently and be 

[11:2:66,378] productive in their communities. Core services consist of information and referral, peer counseling, benefits advocacy, 

[11:3:66,388] independent living skills development, housing assistance, personal assistance services, transition services to community 

[11:4:66,398] based living, transition services to postsecondary life for youth, and personal and systems change advocacy. 

[12:0:66,416] The Department administers and supports the Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI) Program. In coordination with consumers and their 

[12:1:66,426] families, seven service providers throughout California provide a coordinated post-acute care service model for persons with 

[12:2:66,436] TBI, including supported living, community reintegration, vocational supportive services, public awareness, and support for 

[12:3:66,446] family, friends, and professionals within the TBI community. 

[13:0:66,464] The Department administers the federal Older Individuals Who Are Blind program that supports 19 non-profit community-based 

[13:1:66,474] organizations throughout California that provide blindness-related independent living services necessary to assist visually 

[13:2:66,485] impaired consumers age 55 or older to live independently and be productive in their communities. Core services consist of low 

[13:3:66,495] vision training, assistive technology devices and training, orientation and mobility, communication skills, independent living 

[13:4:66,505] skills development, self-advocacy, adjustment counseling, transportation, and supportive services. 

[14:0:66,523] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION 

[15:0:66,540] The Administration Program provides overall management planning, policy development, and administrative support services 

[15:1:66,551] to departmental programs.

[10:0:66,549] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[10:1:66,568] 4250 - STATE COUNCIL SERVICES 

[11:0:66,585] The State Independent Living Council, in conjunction with the Department of Rehabilitation, is responsible for developing a 

[11:1:66,596] state plan for independent living and for monitoring, reviewing and evaluating the implementation of that plan. The Council also 

[11:2:66,606] interacts with similar statewide councils to enhance the effectiveness of the network of centers that provide independent living 

[11:3:66,616] services in California. The Council is required by the Federal Rehabilitation Act of 1973, as amended, in order for the state to 

[11:4:66,626] receive financial assistance for Independent Living Services and the Centers for Independent Living. The Council serves as an 

[11:5:66,636] educational resource on disability and independent living for the Governor, other state agencies, the Legislature, the general 

[11:6:66,647] public, and a variety of statewide and national organizations.

[0:0:66,24] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:407,24] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   175 

[2:0:144,38] 5175   Department of Child Support Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,72] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[3:1:66,91] 4260 - CHILD SUPPORT SERVICES PROGRAM 

[4:0:66,101] The Child Support Services program establishes the system and process for encouraging and, when necessary, enforcing 

[4:1:66,111] parental responsibilities by establishing paternity for children, establishing court orders for financial and medical support, and 

[4:2:66,121] enforcing those orders. The program operates as the single state entity designed to administer the federally mandated Title IV-

[4:3:66,131] D child support program in California. Operation of this program is required for the state to continue to receive the Temporary 

[4:4:66,142] Assistance for Needy Families block grant. 

[4:5:66,159] 4260010 - CHILD SUPPORT ADMINISTRATION: 

[5:0:66,177] The Child Support Administration program provides funding for the salaries and benefits for local and state staff, and operating 

[5:1:66,187] expenses and equipment for the operation of California's child support program, including local child support agencies. The 

[5:2:66,197] federal government provides 66 percent of the funding and the state funds 34 percent of the administration costs. 

[5:3:66,215] 4260019 - CHILD SUPPORT AUTOMATION: 

[6:0:66,233] Pursuant to Federal law, the Department created a single, statewide child support automation system that meets federal 

[6:1:66,243] certification. There are two components of the statewide system: the Child Support Enforcement system and the State 

[6:2:66,253] Disbursement Unit. The enforcement system provides local child support staff tools to manage child support customer accounts 

[6:3:66,263] and locate and intercept assets of non-custodial parents delinquent in their child support payments. The Child Support 

[6:4:66,274] Automation program provides funding for the vendor-operated state disbursement unit, which collects child support payments 

[6:5:66,284] from non-custodial parents and disburses payments to custodial parties. In addition, the Child Support Automation program 

[6:6:66,294] provides funding for electronic data processing maintenance and operation costs at local agencies.

[5:0:66,100] Federal Laws: Social Security Act (Titles II, XVI, XIX). 

[6:0:66,137] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES 

[7:0:65,155] •   End SSI Cash-Out—The Budget includes one-time funding of $230 million General Fund to eliminate the SSI cash-out policy 

[7:1:76,166] no later than August 1, 2019, expanding federal funding for food assistance while holding harmless households potentially 

[7:2:76,176] affected by the change. Prior to this change, SSI individuals did not receive CalFresh benefits and their income was not 

[7:3:76,186] counted in the benefit calculations in a CalFresh household. These individuals instead were given a $10 monthly 

[7:4:76,196] supplemental SSI/SSP benefit. Elimination of this policy results in approximately 370,000 households becoming newly 

[7:5:76,206] eligible for CalFresh benefits, with an additional 45,000 households receiving an increase in CalFresh benefits. 

[8:0:65,223] •   Home Visiting Initiative—The Budget includes $26.7 million for a voluntary CalWORKs Home Visiting pilot program, which 

[8:1:76,233] will provide pregnant women and families with a child under the age of two with home visitation services for up to 24 months, 

[8:2:76,243] with priority given to first-time pregnant women and parents. The goal of the home visiting pilot is to help young families 

[8:3:76,253] reach self-sufficiency by improving family engagement practices, supporting healthy development of young children living in 

[8:4:76,263] poverty, and preparing parents for employment. The pilot will leverage existing, evidence-based program models currently 

[8:5:76,274] being implemented across the state. A total of $131.6 million in one-time federal Temporary Assistance for Needy Families 

[8:6:76,284] block grant funds is being reserved for the pilot's total costs through calendar year 2021. 

[9:0:65,300] •   CalWORKs Grant Increase—The Budget increases CalWORKs grant levels by 10 percent, beginning April 1, 2019, with 

[9:1:76,310] General Fund costs of $90.1 million in 2018-19 and $359.9 million annually thereafter. This increase will bring grant levels to 

[9:2:76,320] 45 percent of the federal poverty level.   Additional increases may be considered beyond 2018-19 until grant levels reach at 

[9:3:76,331] least 50 percent of the federal poverty level. Any such increases would be subject to an appropriation of funds. 

[10:0:65,347] •   CalWORKs Single Allocation Methodology—Compared to the 2017 Budget Act, the Budget includes an increase of $55.8 

[10:1:76,357] million TANF in 2018-19 to reflect the adoption of a revised budgeting methodology for county administration of the 

[10:2:76,367] CalWORKs eligibility determination process. This model recognizes that counties have difficulty adjusting to significant 

[10:3:76,377] increases and decreases in caseload, and attempts to smooth out the changes to county funding.   The methodology: (1) 

[10:4:76,388] establishes a fixed-base funding level that does not adjust when caseload changes, and (2) includes a variable component 

[10:5:76,398] that adjusts when caseload increases or decreases by 5 percent or more, compared to the 2018-19 caseload.   An additional 

[10:6:76,408] one-time $23.5 million General Fund is included for Employment Services, effectively holding the total 2018-19 Single 

[10:7:76,418] Allocation level to the 2017 Budget Act level.   The Administration intends to evaluate the budgeting methodology for the 

[10:8:76,428] Employment Services during 2019-20 budget development. 

[11:0:65,445] •   Safety Net Reserve—The Budget establishes a Safety Net Reserve Fund for CalWORKs and Medi-Cal to maintain program 

[11:1:76,455] services and benefits in economic downturns. The Budget includes an initial transfer of $200 million from the General Fund 

[11:2:76,465] to the Safety Net Reserve Fund, CalWORKs Subaccount. The Department of Finance, in consultation with DSS, DHCS, and 

[11:3:76,475] the Legislative Analyst’s Office, will present a methodology to the Legislature to determine future transfers to and 

[11:4:76,485] distributions from the fund. 

[12:0:65,502] •   IHSS County Administration—The Budget includes $51.8 million General Fund for county IHSS administrative costs in 

[12:1:76,512] 2018-19. The increased funding reflects revised IHSS workload assumptions developed in consultation with representatives 

[12:2:76,522] of counties.   The Budget includes an additional one-time augmentation of $15.4 million General Fund for county 

[12:3:76,532] administration. 

[13:0:65,548] •   Services to Address Homelessness—The Budget includes an augmentation of $24.2 million in 2018-19 to help CalWORKs 

[13:1:76,559] families secure permanent housing, increasing total funding from $47 million to $95 million annually beginning in 2019-20; 

[13:2:76,569] increases the daily payment rate for temporary housing assistance from $65 to $85, effective January 1, 2019, with costs of 

[13:3:76,579] $8.1 million in 2018-19 and $15.3 million annually thereafter; and provides one-time funding of $15 million General Fund to 

[13:4:76,589] establish a three-year pilot program, with local matching funds, designed to provide housing-related supports to seniors 

[13:5:76,599] experiencing or at risk of homelessness. 

[14:0:65,616] •   IHSS Provider Paid Sick Leave—The Budget includes $29.3 million General Fund to reflect implementation of eight paid sick 

[14:1:76,626] leave hours for IHSS providers beginning on July 1, 2018. Accrued paid sick leave hours will increase to 16 hours and 24 

[14:2:76,636] hours annually when the state minimum hourly wage reaches $13 and $15, respectively. General Fund costs are projected 

[14:3:76,646] to grow to $131.2 million by 2022-23. 

[15:0:65,662] •   Immigration Services—The Budget includes a total of $65 million General Fund, including one-time funding of $17 million, for 

[15:1:76,673] the Immigration Services Program to provide a broad array of legal services and remedies for individuals and families related 

[15:2:76,683] to immigration status. The one-time funds will be used primarily to benefit unaccompanied undocumented minors and other 

[15:3:76,693] minors in removal proceedings, current and past beneficiaries of federal temporary protected status, and persons on 

[15:4:76,703] California State University campuses. The Budget also includes $10 million one-time Proposition 98 General Fund to provide 

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,24] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   184 

[1:0:419,24] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:166,38] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,72] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[4:0:66,91] 4270 - WELFARE PROGRAMS 

[5:0:66,108] The Department's public assistance programs provide financial assistance to California residents who are unable to support 

[5:1:66,119] themselves. These programs are comprised of five components: 

[6:0:65,136] •   California Work Opportunity and Responsibility to Kids (CalWORKs) 

[7:0:65,152] •   Other Assistance Payments, including Foster Care, Adoption Assistance Program, Refugee Cash Assistance, and Food 

[7:1:76,163] Assistance Programs 

[8:0:65,179] •   Supplemental Security Income/State Supplementary Payment Program 

[9:0:65,195] •   County Administration and Automation Projects 

[10:0:65,211] •   Disaster Relief 

[11:0:66,229] The objectives of these programs are to provide temporary financial assistance to eligible needy and dependent persons to 

[11:1:66,239] enable achievement of self-sufficiency or to provide safe living environments for vulnerable adults and children, and to monitor, 

[11:2:66,249] administer, and improve the quality of all welfare services. 

[12:0:66,267] 4270010 - CalWORKs: 

[13:0:66,285] The CalWORKs program is California's version of the federal Temporary Assistance for Needy Families program. CalWORKs is 

[13:1:66,295] California's largest cash aid program for children and families and is designed to provide temporary assistance to meet basic 

[13:2:66,305] needs, such as shelter, food, and clothing, in times of crisis, while encouraging personal responsibility. CalWORKs includes 

[13:3:66,315] specific welfare-to-work requirements and provides supportive services, such as child care, to enable an individual to meet 

[13:4:66,326] these requirements. Child care services currently are provided through a three-stage system to current and former CalWORKs 

[13:5:66,336] recipients with children through the age of 10 (or up to 12 under certain conditions). Stage One is administered by the 

[13:6:66,346] Department of Social Services. Stages Two and Three are administered by the California Department of Education. Parents 

[13:7:66,356] have the right to choose child care among center-based, family child care homes, or license-exempt providers. CalWORKs 

[13:8:66,366] families are then able to meet both goals of moving from welfare into the work force and engaging children in child care and 

[13:9:66,377] development services. 

[14:0:66,394] 4270019 - Other Assistance Payments: 

[15:0:66,412] The Foster Care program provides assistance payments to relatives, foster family homes, foster family agencies, short-term 

[15:1:66,422] residential treatment centers or group homes for children who have been removed from the custody of a parent or guardian as 

[15:2:66,432] a result of a judicial order or voluntary placement agreement due to findings of abuse, neglect or exploitation. This program is 

[15:3:66,443] administered by the counties in accordance with regulations, standards, and procedures set by the Department of Social 

[15:4:66,453] Services as authorized by federal and state law. The Kinship Guardianship Assistance Program provides support payments to 

[15:5:66,463] relative guardians of children who were previously in the foster care system. 

[16:0:66,481] The Adoption Assistance Program provides financial assistance to families adopting a child with special needs or to facilitate 

[16:1:66,491] the adoption of children who otherwise would remain in long-term foster care. This program is administered by the counties in 

[16:2:66,501] accordance with regulations, standards, and procedures set by the Department of Social Services as authorized by federal and 

[16:3:66,511] state law. 

[17:0:66,529] California also provides cash assistance to eligible refugee/entrant populations via the following programs: 

[18:0:65,547] •   The Refugee Cash Assistance provides cash grants to refugees/entrants in their first eight months in the United States 

[18:1:76,557] provided they are not otherwise eligible for categorical welfare programs. 

[19:0:65,575] •   The Unaccompanied Refugee Minors program provides culturally and linguistically appropriate child welfare, foster care, and 

[19:1:76,585] independent living services to minors who do not have parents in the United States, or who enter the United States 

[19:2:76,595] unaccompanied by a parent, an immediate adult relative, or an adult having documentable legal evidence of custody of the 

[19:3:76,605] minor. 

[20:0:65,623] •   The Trafficking and Crime Victims Assistance Program provides cash aid and social services to noncitizen victims of human 

[20:1:76,633] trafficking, domestic violence and other serious crimes who meet the income and eligibility requirements. Benefits are 

[20:2:76,643] available for a maximum period of eight months for adults without children and up to 48 months for families (under 

[20:3:76,653] CalWORKs). 

[21:0:66,671] The CalFresh Program, federally referred to as the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program, provides improved levels of 

[21:1:66,681] nutrition among eligible low-income households by offering them a benefit amount, posted to a debit card, for the purpose of 

[21:2:66,692] purchasing food. The cost of CalFresh benefits is provided by the United States Department of Agriculture for populations 

[21:3:66,702] eligible to receive federal benefits. Legal immigrants who meet program eligibility criteria but are ineligible for federal benefits 

[21:4:66,712] due to their immigration status are served under the state-funded program known as the California Food Assistance Program. 

[22:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.
