[3:0:66,65] The CalFresh Employment and Training Program requires certain non-assistance CalFresh recipients to participate in 

[3:1:66,75] employment and training activities. 

[4:0:66,93] The Emergency Food Assistance Program provides commodities to local food banks in all 58 California counties for distribution 

[4:1:66,103] to the working poor, low-income, unemployed, and homeless persons. The food is distributed to eligible recipients for 

[4:2:66,113] household consumption or used to prepare and serve meals in congregate settings. This program is also supplemented with 

[4:3:66,123] food purchased by food banks using private donations, funds provided by the state, taxpayer contributions generated through a 

[4:4:66,134] state income tax check-off, as well as surplus fresh fruits and vegetables donated by farmers and businesses. 

[5:0:66,151] The Commodity Supplemental Food Program is a federally funded program for local non-profit agencies to provide nutritious 

[5:1:66,161] supplemental foods to low-income, elderly people at least 60 years of age. Administrative responsibility for the Commodity 

[5:2:66,172] Supplemental Food Program was transferred from the California Department of Education to the Department of Social Services 

[5:3:66,182] on October 1, 2016. 

[6:0:66,200] 4270028 - Supplemental Security Income/State Supplementary Payment Program: 

[7:0:66,217] The federal Supplemental Security Income (SSI) program is a cash assistance program for low-income aged, blind, or disabled 

[7:1:66,227] persons who meet the program's income and resource requirements. California supplements the federal SSI payment with a 

[7:2:66,238] State Supplementary Payment (SSP). The SSI/SSP program is administered by the federal Social Security Administration who 

[7:3:66,248] determines eligibility, computes grants, and disburses the combined monthly payment to recipients. 

[8:0:66,266] 4270037 - County Administration and Automation Projects: 

[9:0:66,283] Federal, state, and county governments share the cost of operating expenses and the salaries and benefits of county staff who 

[9:1:66,293] administer public assistance programs. 

[10:0:66,311] Federal, state, and county funds are used to finance major data automation projects of the Department of Social Services. 

[11:0:66,329] 4270046 - Disaster Relief: 

[12:0:66,347] The objective of the Disaster Relief Program is to provide monetary assistance to individuals and households who have 

[12:1:66,357] suffered eligible losses from a Presidentially-declared disaster that are not covered by other federal, state, or private assistance 

[12:2:66,367] programs. 

[13:0:66,385] 4275 - SOCIAL SERVICES AND LICENSING 

[14:0:66,402] The Department of Social Services oversees and monitors the administration of social services programs, which include child 

[14:1:66,413] welfare, adoptions, licensing and special programs. The department is responsible for development of policy, regulations, and 

[14:2:66,423] procedures that govern the delivery of services to children, families and other recipients, and the monitoring and evaluation of 

[14:3:66,433] the service delivery system. 

[15:0:66,451] 4275010 - In-Home Supportive Services: 

[16:0:66,468] The In-Home Supportive Services (IHSS) program provides in-home services that enable eligible individuals to remain safely in 

[16:1:66,479] their own homes as an alternative to out-of-home care. Eligible persons are low-income aged, blind, or disabled individuals who 

[16:2:66,489] either qualify for federally funded Medi-Cal or meet the program's income and resource requirements. There are four programs 

[16:3:66,499] that provide in-home care: the Personal Care Services Program, IHSS Plus Option Program, Community First Choice Option, 

[16:4:66,509] and IHSS-Residual Program. 

[17:0:66,527] 4275019 - Children and Adult Services and Licensing: 

[18:0:66,545] The Children's Services component consists of three major areas: Child Welfare Services, Adoptions, and Child Abuse 

[18:1:66,555] Prevention. 

[19:0:66,572] Child Welfare Services provides emergency response, family maintenance, family reunification, and permanent placement and 

[19:1:66,583] prevention services to protect abused, neglected or exploited children. The services are provided through an integrated 

[19:2:66,593] services delivery system that provides intensive services to families to promote child safety, permanency and well-being with 

[19:3:66,603] the goal of allowing families to stay together in their own homes, or arrangement for the child's placement in the safest and 

[19:4:66,613] least restrictive home-like setting. Services also include assistance to youth who are emancipating or have emancipated from 

[19:5:66,623] foster care. The program also provides training and technical assistance to county administrators and staff. 

[20:0:66,641] In Child Welfare Services, the Department of Social Services is implementing continuum of care reforms codified in Chapter 

[20:1:66,651] 773, Statutes of 2015. The reforms emphasize home-based family care, improve access to services without having to change 

[20:2:66,662] out-of-home placements to get those services, and increase the role of children, youth, and families in assessment and case 

[20:3:66,672] planning. 

[21:0:66,689] The Adoptions Program provides support services to children and adoptive families through a collaboration of public and 

[21:1:66,700] private adoption agencies in the state. Agency adoptions provide adoption services through public and private agencies for 

[21:2:66,710] children who have been abused, neglected or exploited and are under the jurisdiction of the county or tribal court. Services 

[22:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[5:3:66,273] 4280 - TITLE IV-E WAIVER 

[6:0:66,291] The Title IV-E California Child Well-Being Project is a federal waiver demonstration project in California. This project provides 

[6:1:66,301] participating counties with a capped federal grant that in turn provides flexibility in the use of federal and state foster care 

[6:2:66,311] maintenance and administrative funds on program and services expenditures that were previously unallowable. 

[6:3:66,329] 4285 - DISABILITY EVALUATION AND OTHER SERVICES 

[7:0:66,347] The objective of this program is to determine an applicant's medical and/or vocational eligibility for disability benefits and 

[7:1:66,357] provide administrative services to other agencies. 

[7:2:66,374] 4285010 - Disability Evaluation: 

[8:0:66,392] The Disability Evaluation Program determines the medical, vocational, and/or functional eligibility of California residents 

[8:1:66,402] applying for benefits under Title II (Disability Insurance), Title XVI (Supplemental Security Income), and Title XIX (Medicaid) of 

[8:2:66,413] the Social Security Act. Eligibility is determined by the severity of the individual's physical and/or mental impairment(s) and 

[8:3:66,423] overall ability to engage in substantial gainful employment. 

[8:4:66,440] 4285019 - Services to Other Agencies: 

[9:0:66,458] In addition to providing support services for its programs, the Department of Social Services provides general administrative 

[9:1:66,468] services, such as personnel and accounting to the State Council on Developmental Disabilities and the Health and Human 

[9:2:66,479] Services Agency. The Department provides services to the Medi-Cal Program in the form of state hearings and public 

[9:3:66,489] information services. 

[9:4:66,506] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION

[1:0:200,43] 5195   State-Local Realignment, 1991 

[2:0:66,64] In the 1991-92 fiscal year, State-Local Program Realignment restructured the state-county partnership by giving counties 

[2:1:66,74] increased responsibilities and funding for a number of health, mental health, and social services programs. This realignment 

[2:2:66,84] provides counties with dedicated tax revenues from the state sales tax and vehicle license fee to pay for these programs.

[1:0:407,24] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   203 

[2:0:165,38] 5195   State-Local Realignment, 1991 - Continued 

[3:0:66,72] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS 

[4:0:66,91] 4350 - STATE-LOCAL REALIGNMENT 

[5:0:66,108] The objectives of Realignment are to assign program responsibility to the most appropriate level of government and achieve 

[5:1:66,119] improved service levels with broad discretion given to the responsible entity. Realignment provides for greater funding stability 

[5:2:66,129] for selected programs, increased local flexibility in administering these programs, and productive fiscal incentives to encourage 

[5:3:66,139] cost-effective approaches to providing services. 

[6:0:66,157] Total Realignment revenues are comprised of a half cent sales tax and a dedicated portion of vehicle license fee revenues. 

[6:1:66,167] Revenues are deposited into the Local Revenue Fund, which includes several accounts. Funds deposited in these accounts 

[6:2:66,177] are continuously appropriated for allocation to local governments according to formula and are used to fund programs specified 

[6:3:66,187] in realignment legislation. The legislation also includes local maintenance of effort and matching requirements in order to 

[6:4:66,197] ensure that counties do not use the realigned funds to supplant local expenditure levels prior to realignment. This provision 

[6:5:66,208] ensures compliance with other state and federal statutes which, in turn, provide hundreds of millions of dollars annually for 

[6:6:66,218] county health and social services programs. 

[7:0:66,258] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES   2018-19 STATE BUDGET — HHS   213 

[1:0:202,43] 5196   2011 State-Local Realignment 

[1:1:66,64] Building upon the 1991-92 Realignment, 2011 Realignment moves program and fiscal responsibility to counties, providing a 

[1:2:66,74] dedicated source of funding while eliminating duplication of effort, generating savings, and increasing flexibility. 

[1:3:66,92] Realigned programs include local public safety programs, mental health, substance abuse, foster care, child welfare services, 

[1:4:66,102] and adult protective services. Many of these programs are already administered at the local level by counties. Therefore, it is 

[1:5:66,112] appropriate for the programmatic and fiscal responsibility to reside with the counties with the state maintaining an oversight and 

[1:6:66,123] technical assistance role where needed. These changes are made with the goal of providing services more efficiently and at 

[1:7:66,133] less cost. 

[1:8:66,150] The funding sources for realignment are: 

[1:9:65,168] •   The dedication of 1.0625 cents of a state special fund sales tax. 

[1:10:65,184] •   The dedication of a portion of vehicle license fee revenues. 

[2:0:66,202] Counties receive 2011 Realignment funding from the following accounts and their related growth accounts: 

[2:1:65,220] •   Protective Services Subaccount (Foster Care, Child Welfare Services, and Adult Protective Services) 

[2:2:65,236] •   Behavioral Health Subaccount (Early and Periodic Screening, Diagnosis, and Treatment; Mental Health Managed Care; 

[2:3:76,246] Substance Abuse Treatment; and Women and Children's Residential Treatment) 

[2:4:65,262] •   Mental Health Account (Community Mental Health Programs) 

[2:5:65,279] •   Trial Court Security Subaccount 

[3:0:65,295] •   Enhancing Law Enforcement Activities Subaccount (Local Jurisdiction for Lower-level Offenders and Parole Violators and 

[3:1:76,305] Adult Parole) 

[3:2:65,321] •   Community Corrections Subaccount 

[3:3:65,337] •   District Attorney and Public Defender Subaccount 

[4:0:65,354] •   Juvenile Justice Subaccount (consisting of the Youthful Offender Block Grant Special Account and Juvenile Reentry Grant 

[4:1:76,364] Special Account) 

[5:0:66,381] The funding reflected below and in the associated special display titled "2011 Realignment Estimate" is an estimate based on 

[5:1:66,392] statutory formulas and the most recent Department of Finance revenue figures. 

[6:0:66,409] Note the $4.9 billion in 2017-18 and $5.1 billion in 2018-19 shown below reflect the Health and Human Services public safety 

[6:1:66,420] programs. This display does not reflect the funding for the non-Health and Human Services public safety programs. For the full 

[6:2:66,430] list of funding in 2011 Realignment, refer to the special display titled "2011 Realignment Estimate."
